Let me create a summary of what I found:\n\n**Kubernetes/kubernetes:**\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` - SetupSignalHandler and SetupSignalContext functions that register SIGTERM/SIGINT handlers. Uses a channel with capacity 2 to handle the case where a second signal is sent, which triggers os.Exit(1).\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` - Defines the shutdownSignals as SIGINT and SIGTERM\n3. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` - Handles graceful termination with:\n   - ShutdownTimeout field (default 2*time.Second for HTTP Server shutdown)\n   - Drains non-long-running requests first\n   - Drains active watches with a grace period\n   - Stops HTTP server gracefully\n   - Runs pre-shutdown hooks\n4. `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` - Similar signal handler to apiserver\n\n**Grafana/grafana:**\n1. `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` - listenToSystemSignals with:\n   - Shuts down background services via managerAdapter\n   - Has timeout handling with context cancellation\n3. `pkg/services/grpcserver/service.go` - gRPC server shutdown:\n   - Initiates graceful stop\n   - Has a timeout (GracefulShutdownTimeout config)\n   - Forcefully terminates if the timeout expires\n\n**Prometheus/prometheus:**\n1. `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - Signal handling:\n Finally, HTTP listeners and server stop\\n\\n**Sample Controller Pattern:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` provides a reusable `SetupSignalHandler()` pattern with the same two-signal approach\\n\\n### Grafana/grafana\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` has `listenToSystemSignals()` function that registers:\\n  - SIGHUP for log reload functionality\\n  - SIGTERM/SIGINT for graceful shutdown via `signal.Notify()`\\n- The handler runs in a goroutine and listens in a select loop for different signals\\n\\n**Shutdown Timeout:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` creates a context with 30-second timeout for shutdown: `context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)`\\n- `pkg/server/server.go` implements the `Shutdown()` method that respects this timeout and handles shutdown failures\\n- `pkg/services/grpcserver/service.go` implements gRPC-specific shutdown with `GracefulShutdownTimeout` configuration (line 195)\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` signal handler (lines 148-170):\\n  1. Signal received (SIGTERM/SIGINT)\\n  2. Create shutdown context with timeout\\n  3. Call `s.Shutdown(ctx, reason)`\\n- `pkg/server/server.go` Shutdown() method (lines 155-172):\\n  1. Stops background services via `managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, \\\"shutdown\\\")`\\n  2. Waits for context to complete or timeout\\n  3. Returns error if shutdown times out\\n- `pkg/services/grpcserver/service.go` gRPC shutdown (lines 184-199):\\n  1. Initiates graceful stop in goroutine\\n  2. Waits for graceful stop to complete OR timeout\\n  3. Forces stop if timeout exceeded\\n\\n### Prometheus/prometheus\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` lines 1154-1177 register SIGTERM and SIGINT handlers using `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)`\\n- Uses the `github.com/oklog/run.Group` pattern for managing multiple goroutines with coordinated shutdown\\n- Termination handler is the first actor in the run.Group, establishing graceful shutdown flow\\n\\n**Shutdown Timeout:**\\n- Implicit timeout handling through `run.Group`: when one actor stops, the cleanup function (second argument to `g.Add()`) is called\\n- Each component's cleanup function handles resource release with appropriate timing\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering (Critical Drain Sequence):**\\nThe `cmd/prometheus/main.go` main() function demonstrates careful shutdown ordering (lines 1150-1600+):\\n\\n1. **Signal Handler (lines 1153-1177):** Registers SIGTERM/SIGINT, initiates shutdown flow\\n2. **Discovery Managers (lines 1179-1204):** Stop scrape and notify discovery managers first to prevent new targets\\n3. **Rule Manager (lines 1207-1219):** Stops before stopping scrape manager to avoid false positives\\n4. **Scrape Manager (lines 1222-1243):** Stopped AFTER rule manager but BEFORE TSDB closure - critical ordering with comment: \\\"Scrape manager needs to be stopped before closing the local TSDB so that it doesn't try to write samples to a closed storage\\\"\\n5. **Tracing Manager (lines 1246-1258):** Stops concurrent with other managers\\n6. **Reload Handler (lines 1261-1343):** Waits for in-progress reloads before stopping\\n7. **Configuration Loading (lines 1346-1374):** Initial config loader stops\\n8. **TSDB/Storage (lines 1376-1435):** Storage closed AFTER all managers that write to it are stopped\\n9. **Remote Storage (cleanup functions):** Closed after scrape manager stops\\n10. **Web Handler (lines 1497+):** Web interface shutdown last\\n\\nThe run.Group pattern ensures that:\\n- Each component's Run() function blocks until its cancel channel closes\\n- The cleanup function for each component is called when the group is interrupted\\n- Cleanup functions can stop dependencies in proper order\\n- All components complete their cleanup before the program exits\\n\\n### Key Patterns Across All Three Services\\n\\n1. **Signal Registration Pattern:** All three use `signal.Notify()` with SIGTERM and SIGINT as primary shutdown signals\\n2. **Context-Based Cancellation:** Both Kubernetes and Grafana use Go contexts with timeouts; Prometheus uses run.Group with cleanup callbacks\\n3. **Two-Signal Handling:** Kubernetes and sample-controller explicitly handle a second signal to force exit\\n4. **Graceful Drain Ordering:** All three implement drain-before-stop patterns:\\n   - Kubernetes: drain requests → drain watches → shutdown HTTP → cleanup\\n   - Grafana: stop services → respect timeout → error on overflow\\n   - Prometheus: stop scrapers → drain storage writes → shutdown TSDB\\n5. **Timeout Management:** All specify explicit shutdown timeouts (Kubernetes: 2-30s, Grafana: 30s, Prometheus: implicit via goroutine cleanup)\"\n}\n","numLines":35,"startLine":1,"totalLines":35}}}
